### Post by CeejRab on 2013-09-15
Hi there stenchbag,

(i feel rude using your name! lol)

This is a pretty easy thing to get around, just run your live CD rather than the install mode and use gparted to view the partitions on the HD. Do what youd like to set it up the way you desire, then reboot and use the install setup. Then you should be able to select the desire partition for the install.

PS: im sure youve thought it through a bit already, but in case you havent... Have you considered running a virtualization machine in your windows 8 install rather than partitioning and dual booting? Its easier in some way, mainly that you dont have to reboot the computer to switch OS's and that its much easier to remove an undesired OS from the virtual machine program than to delete actual partitions and fix boot managers. Just a thought, im not sure where youre coming from so im throwing it out there as a reminder :)

All the best,

---

### Post by CeejRab on 2013-09-15
i figured that was the case that you wanted to test drive it but didnt want to assume too strongly. In that case, virtualization is definitely a better choice than messing with partitions and bootloaders. 

I dont know much about Hyper-V... I would recommend virtualbox, its freeware of course, and runs on all operating systems. Its very easy to use and to remove. Read some instructions on it at their website before starting, and you should be all set! 

I hope you like ubuntu, i was a diehard windows user for years... Now im an apple lover but cant afford it right now although my family has macs, so im using the next best thing, Linux! I have converted to linux ubuntu 12.04 LTS only and im quite happy. (i may even keep ubuntu when i get a mac!) Welcome to the forums by the way lol.

All the best to you,
